<text>The camp ground wasn't anything special at all. If I had one word to describe it, it's would be dirty as there is just bits of trash all over the campground, cordage tied to a bunch of trees, old broken tent poles, you name it, it's there. I had read beforehand that homeless people like to stay here and that is absolutely true. I do not have a problem with homeless people, but what I do have a problem with is that that took up 3 out of the 4 major campgrounds, leaving recreational and backpack users with noot as many options. There is a good water source for filtering and plenty of firewood. Although, it does get quite windy sometimes and the campground sits right in the middle of an open canyon. I would come back if I had to, but this wouldn't be my first choice.< /text>< pics>

<rating>4< /rating>< Review>
Proximity and ease of entry make it a great overnight spot. Bike packed in with a buddy, we rolled just hammocks and it was no problem. 5ish fire pits. No water. There are toilets. Great place to shake down your gear and test it out before you head into real wilderness. Note though it is a free and open camp ground and attracts some interesting people, transient types camp here year around so just keep your wits about ya and it'll be fine.< /Review>

<user_name>Andy K< /user_name><date>1474558811739</date>< Rate>
5</Rate>
<review>One of my favorite hikes in all of Los Angeles. The trail is accessible by the camp site, but also from Switzer Falls and near JPL. It is well shaded and hugs the stream, if there is enough water.

The camp site is down a mile long fire road, so pack accordingly, especially because you'll have to walk back up the steep hill.

For a better back packing excursion, start the Gabrielino Trail near JPL, it is a good hike from there to the campground. If you want to do hard mode, start the gabrielino trail near Switzer. It is a good 9 mile hike along the arroyo secco, through some mountains, valleys, and an old river bed. With camping gear, it will be a great adventure.< /review><pictures>None<//pictures>< Response>
None< /Response>

<gmap_id>0x80c2e9c3d87eda8b:0x9a9691975d09c4fa< /gmap_id><review>The last time I was there was about 25 years ago. This is a backpacker's campsite; in other words, the public cannot drive to it; you must backpack in or ride a horse in. When I was there, there was a ranger that lived in a trailer. There is a community of rangers that live nearby. This is a great place to hike to; it is an easy walk. The trail roughly parallels the stream. There is opportunity for shade along the trail from (near) JPL. There is a relatively large pool in the stream next to the camp.

If you continue up the trail you can go all the way to Oakwilde Picnic Area which is also a backpacker's campsite. The trail is easy except for the part that goes past a dam. I think that is in the area of the Paul Little Campground.

If you continue up from Oakwilde then the trail becomes relatively steep. It goes up to the Switzer Picnic area.< /review>< Name>
Sam Hobbs<//Name>

<Date>1494238698548</Date><user>107434908954743368047<//user>< gmap_id>
0x80c2960bb5ecac33:0xf3623bbb80e1b13b</gmap_id>
<pictures>None<//pictures><Name>Stocks Huskies (Stocks and Huskies)<//Name>< Rate>
1< /Rate>

None<//Resp>
< text>
There are two facts here. This place was overpriced and we were underwhelmed.

We ordered 3 burritos, all wet:  2 chicken (I requested specifically to make them as SPICY as they can), 1 carne.  They were served with sour cream on the side and decent rice.  I didn't think we would need salsa because they were all wet, so I asked for none.  The beans were pureed to paste ... yet that would help for the arduous task ahead.

We all came to the agreement that the wet burritos are not seasoned correctly nor does the 'wetness' help these meals' inherent dryness.  The beans HAD to be mixed in because otherwise you would end up choking to get the burrito down.  They even had Cilantro in them ... which is all you tasted when you came across a leaf of it ...  We added salt to the beans and Tapatio and salsa, from our house, to these bricks to get some semblance of flavor... to no avail.  This food was a lost cause. It was like eating wet Army MREs.

I actually stopped in the middle of my burrito because I didn't want any more ... yet, I was still hungry.  I've only been that confused several times in my life ... how do I have food that I paid for, yet not want to eat???

This was compounded by the fact that all three burrito meals came out to be $40, yet we were given one bag of chips with 14 chips in it (nope, not a typo ... 14 chips, we counted).  I see now why they only gave us 14 chips ... we could barely get the burritos down, what would the chips do??

So, $40 ... for three burrito meals ... for slow take out Mexican ... basically, West Hollywood prices for food that tastes like bland Golden Corral ... yeah, won't be eating here again.

There is no way that the other 'good' reviewers are reviewing this place;  they may be talking about the other one on Lakersham that is also within 1 mile - not here.  I believe some of the other 'good' reviews are based on laziness, availability and the ability to order online delivery.  These reviews should review the food and not the fact that the delivery service delivered it to your door.

Also, there were two people that said it was the best Mexican food they've ever eaten while they were walking out (like they were trying to convince everyone that was there) ... they either don't get out much or they're lying to help the place.  I don't like liars because that is the reason I tried this nonsense in the first place.

I hate putting in a bad review because the women who make the food are very nice.  Yet, the food itself leaves a LOT to be desired.  Don't be swayed by the 5 star reviews; I think you would come out better driving through Taco Bell.< /text>

<Rating>5</Rating><Review>I remember seeing this bridge back in 1973, while on vacation with my family when I was eight years old.  I never knew exactly where it was located, but it always held my interest.  I sometimes would think about this other red California suspension bridge.  Now, thanks to the internet, I know it to be the Guy West Pedestrian Suspension Bridge. It is a 1/7th scaled mini replica of the Golden Gate Bridge.<//Review>< Pics>
None</Pics>
<resp>None< /resp><gmap_id>0x809adaf2ff91eafb:0x10cc6379635b3b14< /gmap_id></record></dataset><record>
<UserId.>111674502068205069646< /UserId.><username>Aaron Fleming< /username><time>1615271287611</time><rating>5</rating>< Review>
The views from Guy West Bridge, depending on the time, are extremely scenic. Some might say breathtaking! I fish from this bridge regularly. There are almost always Sac state students going either to or from school. It is also a favorite crossing point for the elite biking community in the area. Every one is always so friendly and respectful! Amazing photos can be taken here! Wonderful birds eye view of the American River! Nature lovers welcome!!
However swimmers beware!! The pics in this review are of a 400 + pound sea lion who regularly chase the larger salmon and steelhead through the river. When they catch them the sight is quite gruesome! The fish are ripped apart by the sea lion flinging them back and forth, slapping them on the water several times until one half goes flying. They then choke down half of a sometimes 26 pound fish then race off to get the other half. While fishing on the Sac river one day, a friend and i witnessed this up close and personal. The sea lion paid no mind to our boat, ramming into it while chasing what appeared to be several Salmon. We were jolted violently as the huge animal nearly capsized our boat! They are relentless eaters and i have no doubt a human being would be in serious danger if in the water with one. They are amazingly fast swimmers so my advice is DO NOT SWIM IN THE SAC OR AMERICAN DURING SALMON SEASON. And if ur fishing during that time dont hang ur catch off the side of ur vessel!</Review>

< Text>
With current concerns over light pollution in cities, it seems obvious that the Guy West Bridge "renovation" neglected to consult anyone with a forward thinking perception of the issue, let alone any possible aesthetic sensibility. What used to be a pleasant evening stroll to view the river and the night sky from the bridge is now a glaring blast of LED spotlights that make you want to shield your eyes, a gross oversight to such a handsome bridge.< /Text>

< review>
I like it because it's local but it's expensive compared to other beauty supplies and they don't allow returns or exchanges..

I don't like doing business anywhere I can't return or at least exchange an item... I bought hair for braiding that I ended up not being able to use because my braider said it would cut her fingers....It was never opened and I had the receipt and they wouldn't let me bring it back so I'm stuck with five packs of hair that I can never use...

If it was a wig or something I could see, but something in a package that has clearly never been opened you should at least be able to exchange!

This is a policy that is typical of a lot of Asian Merchants which is why I don't do swap meets and don't really like to patronize them because it's not the American way...

So due to their no exchange policy, I will not be shopping there again..< /review>

< review>
This is a great spot - the concept is great, atmosphere is great the food is great. I am giving 3 stars because this place needs to really replace some of its staff members. Where are the smiles? I mean, give me a break! From some of them I get the vibe that they don't even care much. Also cleanliness in a food outlet is a must!  Some staff members look unkempt wearing whatever clothes and unclean. I get it that it's a casual spot, but you are touching my food and must have clean hands, clean clothes and maybe even gloves. Handle my food with love and care -  you are not doing me a favor preparing it! Job is a job - if it were a free or 1 buck eatery like Taco bell, I would care less and be happy with whatever and however you serve it to me. Definitely like the place but won't be back until these issues addressed.<//review>

I admit I only visited this place because I had a $5 coupon for it, but I was pleasantly surprised. Granted, all I had was some fruit because coffee makes me ill, and anyone would be hard pressed to mess up a plate of seasonal plant ovaries (which is what fruit is - think about it). <user_id>111076956788798183516</user_id>< username>
Paul Bulger< /username>
<time>1508642327366<//time>< Rate>
5</Rate>
< Review>
If you're a movie buff wading through the $1.95 "buy ten get five free" section, you'll come across piles and piles of garbage. But be patient. Be persistent. Amongst all the muck, there's hundreds of little diamonds waiting to be uncovered, and sometimes the thrill of those discoveries are truly exhilarating. Pictured are 45 movies I found and got for less than 60 bucks one time. This doesn't even include some of the best stuff I've found on other days I've gone. I don't know of any other place in Fresno that deals in physical media with more value to the dollar than Rasputin's.

In addition to movies, I've also purchased quite a few records here. The value to the dollar you get for music is not as exciting as it is for the movies, but the selection is still excellent, and you'd have to scour thrift shops in Clovis to find a better selection of records than you'll find here.</Review>

< review>
Rasputin has the best hip hop collection out of all the record stores in town that I have went to. Not only that, but they have newer releases that other stores might be slacking on. They have some pretty special vinyls for anyone looking to collect. They have a good CD collection as well, but its pretty clear that rock is what Rasputin majors in. If you want rock, then just go here. They have something for everyone. Don't know if they have an anime section, but I wouldn't be surprised if they did. A lot of DVDs a person can buy too. Basically a collector of physical media. Don't really know about their service because I work better when people let me focus on what vinyls and CDs I want to buy, but its probably alright.< /review>

<userid>102703121488514444617</userid>< username>
The Reviewer<//username>
< Date>
1422058379677<//Date>
<rating>2</rating>< review>
As you walk into the establishment, you may (probably not, though) be greeted with an almost inaudible, "...hello." by one of the less-than-helpful staff. Upon searching through their selections of CDs, you may notice that they are merely MOSTLY alphabetized with random "D"s in the "C" categories, etc. Although the aforementioned lack of knowledge concerning the alphabet is indeed frustrating, it is the least of your worries. The next issue of concern is the actual price of their merchandise. Unless you are buying used items (even then, it may still break your wallet), be prepared to be high-balled out of your hard-earned cash. Granted, you may occasionally find something for under $7, but chances are the item - assuming its a disc - will be scratched to hell (hence, the reduced pricing). Moving on: if you plan on selling any VHS tapes, cassette tapes, CDs, DVDs, or Video Games, be prepared to be mocked with a smug scoff or out-loud chuckle. Also, make sure you weren't planning on buying anything with the money you assumed you would get, because they pay you literal pennies (I had planned on selling some video games around Christmas and - to my dismay - I was offered 5 cents for the majority of my items). In summary, sell your things on Amazon or eBay. Next issue of concern: don't bother applying for a job there. Not only does the establishment not take applications (literally...they don't have Rasputin Records job applications), but I've also been tipped off by a reliable ex-employee who informed me that they hire within a limited circle of friends, the "Rasputin family" network as it were. Nepotism at its finest. Lastly, the employees: the majority of the staff are rude and virtually unknowing about the availability of music in stock. Don't bother asking to see if something is in stock. You are better off looking yourself. Rasputin assumes a virtual monopoly of music in Fresno, and they are aware. Don't support Corporate America. Buy whatever you are searching for online.</review>
